# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox CSS Style Resolution to Layout Paint Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a CSS style change triggers layout and paint in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the style change notification, the frame style recomputation, the dirty-frame reflow scheduling, the display list construction, and the WebRender layer update.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

I've completed a comprehensive trace of how CSS style changes trigger layout and paint in Mozilla Firefox. The analysis includes all the key C++ source files implementing the five major stages:

## Summary of the CSS Style Change to Paint Chain

**Created `/workspace/answer.json`** with:

1. **25 key source files** including:
   - Style system: `RestyleManager.cpp`, `ServoStyleSet.cpp`, `nsChangeHint.h`
   - Layout/reflow: `PresShell.cpp`, `nsIFrame.cpp`
   - Display lists: `nsDisplayList.cpp`, `nsDisplayList.h`
   - WebRender integration: `WebRenderLayerManager.cpp`, `WebRenderCommandBuilder.cpp`, `RenderRootStateManager.cpp`

2. **15 critical symbols** representing key functions and classes in the pipeline

3. **Complete call chain** showing the flow from DOM style notification through WebRender compositor updates

4. **Detailed narrative** explaining:
   - How Element style changes notify RestyleManager
   - How frames are restyled via Servo style engine integration
   - How dirty bits schedule reflow via PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow()
   - How display lists are constructed from the frame tree
   - How WebRenderCommandBuilder transforms display lists into WebRender commands
   - How WebRenderBridgeParent sends the final display list to the compositor

The answer captures the complete propagation path from a CSS style change through frame style recomputation, dirty frame scheduling, display list construction, and finally to WebRender layer compositing.

The process can be traced through several key stages:\\n\\n**Stage 1: Style Change Notification**\\nWhen a CSS style changes (e.g., via element.style or attribute modifications), Element::NotifyStyleStateChange() and Element::NotifyStateChange() in dom/base/Element.cpp trigger notifications. These call into RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent() in layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp, which posts a restyle event to the pres context.\\n\\n**Stage 2: Frame Style Recomputation**\\nThe RestyleManager::ProcessRestyledFrames() function in layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp is the core of style recomputation. It processes the nsStyleChangeList (defined in layout/style/nsStyleChangeList.cpp) which collects all frames affected by the style change along with their nsChangeHint values (from layout/style/nsChangeHint.h). The ServoStyleSet in layout/style/ServoStyleSet.cpp integrates with the Servo style engine to recalculate computed styles. For each frame with a new computed style, nsIFrame::DidSetComputedStyle() is called (layout/generic/nsIFrame.cpp), allowing frames to react to style changes.\\n\\n**Stage 3: Dirty Frame and Reflow Scheduling**\\nBased on the nsChangeHint values, PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow() in layout/base/PresShell.cpp schedules frames for reflow. The change hints (like nsChangeHint_NeedReflow, nsChangeHint_NeedDirtyReflow, nsChangeHint_RepaintFrame) determine the type of reflow needed. Frame dirty bits such as NS_FRAME_IS_DIRTY and NS_FRAME_HAS_DIRTY_CHILDREN (defined in layout/generic/nsFrameStateBits.h) are set to mark frames requiring reflow or repaint.\\n\\n**Stage 4: Display List Construction**\\nDuring the paint phase, nsDisplayListBuilder in layout/painting/nsDisplayList.cpp walks the frame tree and constructs a display list of painting instructions. Each frame's BuildDisplayList() method (in layout/generic/nsIFrame.cpp) is called to contribute display items. The nsDisplayList.h header defines the various nsDisplayItem types that represent visual elements to be rendered. InvalidateFrame() methods in nsIFrame.cpp mark regions as needing repainting.\\n\\n**Stage 5: WebRender Layer Update**\\nThe WebRenderLayerManager in gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderLayerManager.cpp receives the constructed display list and calls EndTransactionWithoutLayer(). The WebRenderCommandBuilder in gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderCommandBuilder.cpp transforms the display list into WebRender commands through CreateWebRenderCommandsFromDisplayList(). The RenderRootStateManager in gfx/layers/wr/RenderRootStateManager.cpp manages the WebRender backend state and resource updates. Finally, the WebRenderBridgeParent in gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderBridgeParent.cpp receives the display list data via SetDisplayList() and sends it to the WebRender compositor on the compositor thread for rendering.\\n\\nThis chain demonstrates how a single CSS style change propagates from DOM mutation through layout invalidation, frame reflow, display list construction, and finally to WebRender compositing for efficient multi-threaded rendering.\"\n}\n",
